## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration A, which is a classic chemical kinetics problem. The rate law typically depends on concentration raised to some power (reaction order), and may involve complex mechanisms like autocatalysis or reversible reactions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Mixed order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (substrate inhibition or saturation)
- Second-order with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A) (rate with self-inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent rate constant)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order reaction, e.g., surface reactions)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Quadratic with constant: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (general second-degree polynomial rate law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate proportional to concentration power → n-th order irreversible decomposition: dA_dt = -c * A**n
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction or equilibrium: terms like c0*A + c1 indicate forward/backward balance
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where product concentration drives reaction
- Rate that levels off at high concentration → saturation kinetics, use rational functions A/(1+c*A) rather than pure power laws
- Exponential time dependence in rate → time-varying rate constant, possibly due to temperature ramp or catalyst deactivation
- Rate with half-integer power of concentration → surface-mediated or diffusion-limited reaction mechanism
- Linear relationship between dA_dt and A → first-order kinetics, check for nonzero intercept indicating reversibility or constant source/sink
- Curvature in log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) plot → fractional or mixed-order kinetics, slope gives effective reaction order

**GT:** `-0.4466*A*exp(-0.0866*t) + 0.9910*sin(sqrt(A))`

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A*exp(-0.0866*t)` (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
2. A term `sin(sqrt(A))` (no t dependence)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce exactly these two basis functions: `A*exp(αt)` and `sin(√A)`.

Key observations:
- `sin(√A)` is a very specific nonlinear function. It cannot be represented by polynomials in A, `log(A+1)`, `exp(A)`, `A^c`, or other common functions.
- `sin(√A)` can potentially be written as `sin(c*log(A*c + 1))` only if `c*log(c*A+1) = √A`, which is not generally true.
- The only way to get `sin(√A)` is to have `sin(√A)` explicitly or something algebraically equivalent.

Let me check candidates that contain `sin` with arguments that could equal `√A`:

**Candidate 9:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`
The sin argument is `c5*log(A*c6+1) + c7`. For this to equal `√A`, we'd need `c5*log(c6*A+1) = √A` for all A, which is impossible (log vs sqrt).
Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 46:** `A²*c0 + c1 + c2*t/(A+c3)^5 + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6+1) + c7)`
Same issue with sin(log(...)) ≠ sin(√A).
Candidate 46 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 63:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6) + c7`
sin(A*c5 + c6) ≠ sin(√A).
Candidate 63 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 61:** `(c0 + c1*(c2*exp(c3*t)+1)*sin(A*c4+c5))/(c2*exp(c3*t)+1)`
This simplifies to `c0/(c2*exp(c3*t)+1) + c1*sin(A*c4+c5)`. sin(linear in A) ≠ sin(√A).
Candidate 61 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 74:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A*c5+1) + c6)`
sin(log(...)) ≠ sin(√A).
Candidate 74 verdict: [NO MATCH]
